  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d3098fc0-95b9-4ac3-b536-330cd5a2bf1a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText7381628533712147057" style="display:none">Tanner Layne and Raquel Merrick fell in love young, hard and fast and both of them knew a beautiful life they thought would be forever. <br /><br />Until Rocky left Layne, no explanation, no going back. <br /><br />Layne escapes The ‘Burg only to come back years later because his ex-wife has hooked herself to the town jerk and Layne needs to make sure his sons get raised right. Layne manages to avoid Rocky but when Layne gets three bullets drilled into him while investigating a dirty cop, he can’t do that because Rocky stops avoiding Layne. They make a deal to work together to expose the dirty cop but they have no idea the strength of their enduring attraction or the sheer evil at work in The ‘Burg. <br /><br />As Tanner Layne and Raquel Merrick play their game and dance around the pull that draws them together, Layne has to discover the dark secrets buried so deep in Rocky’s heart she doesn’t even know they’re there at the same time untangle a sinister web of crime so abhorrent it has to be stopped... at all costs. <br /><br />And to do it, Layne has to enlist everyone, including his ex-CIA mentor, Rocky’s detective brother, the town’s unpredictable informant and Layne’s two teenage sons all the while stopping Rocky from doing something crazy and keeping their game secret so Layne won't get himself dead.</span>

<div id="review_1650988812" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1650988812" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1650988812?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=hated-it">hated-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=alpha-asshole">alpha-asshole</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=characters-i-want-to-torture-maim">characters-i-want-to-torture-maim</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=buddy-read-with-bbbs">buddy-read-with-bbbs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1650988812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14880872007111960820"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464576729i/19252438.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I think Kristen Ashley's alpha assholes are the picture of mansplaining. Reading one of her books will send feminists into homicidal rages, and would even be good propaganda material to recruit for the cause. <br/><br/>Here is a typical conversation in a KA book:<br/><br/><b>Girl:<i> I really need to talk to you about your actions last night. When you grabbed me by the wrist and threw me against the wall, it really hurt. I had to go to the hospital after you finally let me leave this morning and - </i><br/><br/>Guy:<i> Come and listen to</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText14880872007111960820" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464576729i/19252438.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think Kristen Ashley's alpha assholes are the picture of mansplaining. Reading one of her books will send feminists into homicidal rages, and would even be good propaganda material to recruit for the cause. <br><br>Here is a typical conversation in a KA book:<br><br><b>Girl:<i> I really need to talk to you about your actions last night. When you grabbed me by the wrist and threw me against the wall, it really hurt. I had to go to the hospital after you finally let me leave this morning and - </i><br><br>Guy:<i> Come and listen to my story about a man named Jed.</i><br><br>Girl:<i> Would you please let me finish! I can't continue this abusive relationship! I am breaking - </i><br><br>Guy:<i> A poor mountaineer, barely kept his family fed, </i><br><br>Girl: <i>Guy, listen to - </i><br><br>Guy: <i>And then one day he was shootin at some food,</i><br><br>Girl:<i> Guy!!!</i><br><br>Guy:<i> And up through the ground come a bubblin crude.</i><br><br>Girl: <i>Okay. Whatever you say. You are so much smarter than me. I will have sex with you now.</i></b><br><br>Alright, I admit that maybe the guy isn't exactly reciting the theme song from the '70's TV show, The Beverly Hillbillies, but he might as well be. Because it doesn't really matter what he says, the point is that he's right and she's wrong. In everything. In this book, our male "hero" explains to his woman why she shouldn't have her own feelings about her period. She's in her late 30's.<br><br>That's right. Our man mansplained menstruation to a woman!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464576729i/19252439._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Another common thread is that the male alphas typically think their female is "cute" when she's angry. So, when the woman is angry because he has done or said something extremely horrible (which is often), the man will typically laugh or decide to force sexual advances on her. He can't help himself! She's sexy when she's mad!<br><br>You know what else is cute when mad? Babies. We, as their parents see those little face bottom lips go out and it's so adorable.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464576729i/19252440._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>See? That's cute!<br><br>Do we consider babies our intellectual equals? No. Do we think that our opinion means more than a baby's? Of course. Do we make babies do what we need them to do despite their complaints? Yes. They have to go to bed at night, allow us to change their diaper - even if we have to hold them down, and get dressed - even though it means that we have to manipulate their arms and legs into the clothing for them.<br><br>The problem is that the men typically do all of the above to their women. The woman is below the man in every way. Her opinion is unimportant compared to his. She is forced to have physical contact with him against her will. She is constantly being manipulated by him in every way.<br><br>And, the conversations between the characters is excruciating! Here is a snippet from the book. Let's see if you can get through it without wanting to kill someone:<br><br><b>
  <i>"Why?" he asked.<br>"Why?" she repeated.<br>"yes. Why?"<br>"Layne, I'm not sure we should -"<br>"Why?"<br>"I really don't want to talk about - "<br>"Why?"<br>"Layne!"<br>He leaned in to get his face close to hers. "Why?" he repeated.<br>"Why do you want to know?" she shot back.<br>"Because I do," he answered.</i>
</b><br><br>I bet you find that conversation irritating, huh? Well, the book is filled with these little ditties. Pages and pages of them. Seriously, if these type of exchanges were omitted from the book, it would probably shrink it in half.<br><br>And, in this book we had a "hero" with teenage sons. God help us all! He thinks it is perfectly acceptable for his 14-yr old and 17-yr old sons to say "fuck" around him and his woman. His oldest son is a complete manwhore and he is all proud of him with a "that's my boy" attitude until the son meets "the right girl". Then, he tells his son that he has to treat her right and not step out on her. Well, of course! Those other teen girls that his son screwed are not deserving of respect or decency! Only "the right girl" deserves to be treated well. The rest of those girls deserved to be screwed and screwed over. They deserved to have their hearts broken and hopes unfulfilled. What a bunch of sluts they must have been to have allowed the most popular boy in school, the football hero of the town, sweet-talk them into sex. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464576729i/19252441.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Time to man-up and drink a beer, boy!<br><br>He also decides that his 14-yr old son will work undercover against a pedophile who is running a sex ring. This is the same pedophile that he refuses to allow his woman to even talk to because he is so dangerous. So, in other words, an adult woman is less capable of keeping herself safe than a 14-yr old boy? Evidently.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464576729i/19252442._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Of course, his ex-wife is a bitch. A dumb bitch. So, any problems she has with his style of parenting is just too bad. He is the man. He is the fathering genius. Sure, he was gone for the first 12 years of their lives while she had to do it all alone, but he's around now. That means that he is in charge. Stand back, women!! A man is here now! He'll take it from here.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464576729i/19252443._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, even though I have had an awesome time reading these books with all of my reading buddies in the BBB group, I don't know if I can go on. I get way too stabby when I read these. I live in a home with two sons and a husband and I am just not sure if I can keep a male alive in my home when I read these books. Anything with a penis is in danger around me right now.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459543412i/18624780.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14880872007111960820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_481613823" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/481613823" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/481613823?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer481613823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1351050640064582568"><b>4-4.5 Golden stars!!!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/ad41833c-4fe1-4815-96b1-f86a2658363a_zps3044065e.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404302261i/10222365.jpg' alt=' photo ad41833c-4fe1-4815-96b1-f86a2658363a_zps3044065e.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I’ve never read a Kristen Ashely book I didn’t like. <i>Golden Trail</i> was no exception. I loved Layne and Rocky’s second chance love story! <br/><br/>Eighteen years. That’s how long it’s been since the love of Tanner Layne’s life up and left him. Raquel Merrick. Rocky. She was the one for him. They were happy and in love, until one day she was gone. Since then, Layne has had two boys- Jasper and Tripp, who are both teenagers. He’s been married, then divorced. He’s traveled all over fo</span>
  <span id="freeText1351050640064582568" style="display:none"><b>4-4.5 Golden stars!!!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/ad41833c-4fe1-4815-96b1-f86a2658363a_zps3044065e.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404302261i/10222365.jpg" alt=" photo ad41833c-4fe1-4815-96b1-f86a2658363a_zps3044065e.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I’ve never read a Kristen Ashely book I didn’t like. <i>Golden Trail</i> was no exception. I loved Layne and Rocky’s second chance love story! <br><br>Eighteen years. That’s how long it’s been since the love of Tanner Layne’s life up and left him. Raquel Merrick. Rocky. She was the one for him. They were happy and in love, until one day she was gone. Since then, Layne has had two boys- Jasper and Tripp, who are both teenagers. He’s been married, then divorced. He’s traveled all over for work and now he’s back and settled in the Burg to be near his sons. He tries not to think too much about Rocky, but it’s hard now. She’s infiltrated his job and his life. <br><br>Rocky is determined to help take down a dirty cop. She has her reasons for wanting to help, but Layne can’t let her do this alone. He still cares about her and he doesn’t want to see her hurt. For this operation to work, they have to ‘pretend’ to be back together. Since Layne is single and Rocky is in the middle of a divorce, it works. Layne thinks he hates Rocky. Hates her for leaving him, for what she put him through. But with time, he realizes it’s the exact opposite. <br><i>
  <blockquote>Layne knew he was in love with her. Not only that, he’d never stopped loving her. Not once, not for a second, not for twenty-one years.<br>Fuck him.</blockquote>
</i> Layne and Rocky aren’t just dealing with their feelings for one another, they also have so much more than they bargained for in this case they’re working. Bad things are going down in the Burg and they’re working to solve the mystery of whats going on. As they continue to work the case, Rocky grows closer to Layne and his boys. Layne comes to find the reason Rocky really left. Their ‘fake’ relationship turns more real day by day. Neither had lost the feelings they’ve always had for one another. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/598f3c1e-9af3-4ffb-acbd-1d5928f1f9d8_zps31295d09.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404302261i/10222366.jpg" alt=" photo 598f3c1e-9af3-4ffb-acbd-1d5928f1f9d8_zps31295d09.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“What am I gonna do with you, Raquel Merrick?”<br><br> “Anything you want, Layne. As long as you’re with me when you do it.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br>One of my favorite things about this one- it was 100% written in Layne’s pov. Love books written in the males perspective. Especially when it’s a KA male. <br><br>Layne was a wonderful hero. That is one of the best words I could use to describe the man. HERO. What a guy! He’s a stand up man, great father, kind, considerate, but still that possessive and sexy alpha male. And his sons… I fell in love with them both! Jasper, just like a mini Layne, and Tripp who was the sweetest! Couldn’t get enough of the Layne boys! I loved what Jasper said when he first started dating Kiera (Joe Cal’s step-daughter)<br><i>
  <blockquote>“It’s good she hooked up with me, she’s such a nut, she needs a badass to take her back.”</blockquote>
</i> Then Tripp talking about trying to get with Giselle. <br><i>
  <blockquote>“Giselle Speakmon’s parents are totally devout. When I get in there and we hook up, there won’t be any cribs for me either, Dad, because I reckon they’ll make me wear one of those chastity belts, knowin’ Jas is my brother and all.” </blockquote>
</i> They made me smile and laugh out loud so many times. Ryker was also a fun character, and Rocky’s brother Merry. I’m looking forward to his book!<br><br>Rocky was one of those heroines I wasn’t sure about in the beginning of the book, but she grew on me. I didn’t understand her at first. What her reasons were for the things she did in the past, and to be honest I just didn’t like her much because she broke Layne’s heart all those years ago. But the more I got to ‘know’ her character, saw how she was with the boys, her students, and saw how much she truly did love Layne, I started to really like her. By the end of the story, she won me over. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/ed1c6f56-9f52-4805-82a4-cdf6fd059a6a_zpsa59e8377.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404302261i/10222367.jpg" alt=" photo ed1c6f56-9f52-4805-82a4-cdf6fd059a6a_zpsa59e8377.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>The only reason I didn’t give it 5… I felt like there were parts in the middle that dragged. I don’t mind that most of KA’s books are long, in fact, I love that about her stories. It’s just some of the middle felt like it was unnecessary and I had a few moments that I was a little bored. Luckily, the bulk of the story captivated me so it wasn’t a big issue. <br><br>I love Kristen Ashely’s writing. That woman has a way with words. I fall in love with every book of hers I read. Most every character too. With how courageous and brave Layne was, it was difficult not to love him. Her ‘The Burg’ series is great because it’s not only romance, but it’s packed full of family, friendship, mystery and suspense. There is always so much going on, but it always comes together in the best way by the end. You will laugh, cry, swoon, and be moved when reading one of her books. This is a series I adore and I’m looking forward to jumping into the next one asap! <br><i>
  <blockquote>“Live this with me, just life it. Whatever happens, however it happens, just live it with me.”</blockquote>
</i><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/4f0a3620-f1f2-44f8-b4e2-bb02e01abe68_zps464f7659.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404302261i/10222368.jpg" alt=" photo 4f0a3620-f1f2-44f8-b4e2-bb02e01abe68_zps464f7659.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And my favorite quote… because it’s SO TRUE!<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“See, that's the beauty of books. We get to take what we want out of them and it can be different for everyone. You get a good one, you may even find what you need.” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1351050640064582568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_314595829" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/314595829" />
    <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole"><img alt="Duchess Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499265843p2/2204947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/314595829?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duchess Nicole" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole">Duchess Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=e-pcs">e-pcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=2-star-read">2-star-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=ebooks-i-own-smashwords">ebooks-i-own-smashwords</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=dirty-talk">dirty-talk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=heroine-tstl">heroine-tstl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=highly-rated">highly-rated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-contemp-romance">genre-contemp-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-romantic-suspense">genre-romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=angsty">angsty</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer314595829" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3415445804804033303">Prevaricate...<br/>Equivocate...<br/>Evade...<br/>Evade...<br/>Evade...<br/><br/>I always feel defensive when I don't like a Kristen Ashley book. And I always feel as if I should be very thorough about my expectations, my history with the author, and whatever the hell happened with this particular experience.<br/><br/><i>Yeah, really...what the heck happened, Duchess?</i><br/><br/>Well, you see, I'm not really sure. Everything about this book just rubbed me wrong. Maybe it was bad timing, maybe I've read one too many alpha male stories. Maybe I grew t</span>
  <span id="freeText3415445804804033303" style="display:none">Prevaricate...<br>Equivocate...<br>Evade...<br>Evade...<br>Evade...<br><br>I always feel defensive when I don't like a Kristen Ashley book. And I always feel as if I should be very thorough about my expectations, my history with the author, and whatever the hell happened with this particular experience.<br><br><i>Yeah, really...what the heck happened, Duchess?</i><br><br>Well, you see, I'm not really sure. Everything about this book just rubbed me wrong. Maybe it was bad timing, maybe I've read one too many alpha male stories. Maybe I grew tired of the KA formula. To defend myself a bit, the previous book in this series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11665750.At_Peace__The__Burg___2_" title="At Peace (The 'Burg, #2) by Kristen Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">At Peace</a>, is one of my all time favorite books. So it's not that I'm growing tired of KA, I don't think. It was just these characters and this book, the intensely serious subject matter and the New Adult dramatics that inundated the pages.<br> <img src="https://www.goodreads.com/image..." width="40" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b>
  <i>-- Layne wasn't alpha. He was an overbearing, know it all jackass. </i>
</b> I know this is typical for KA but I felt it was so overdone here. Layne can do no wrong, Layne is the best, the strongest, the hottest, the fastest. <br><br><b>
  <i>-- Raquel (Rocky) wasn't a strong woman. She was feeble and weak willed.</i>
</b> The only thing I liked about Rocky was her passion for literature. Other than that, she caves to Layne's pushy, obnoxious ways...but always puts up a fake fight, just enough to be annoying. I'm not even sure how many times this convo happened but I started wishing they were real just so I could smack them the next time they said this:<br><br>"I can pay for dinner, Layne."<br>"I know you can, you just aren't."<br>"Layne."<br>"Rocky."<br>"Layne."<br>"Roc."<br>"Layne!"<br>...and then he does what he wants to anyways. Some variation of that happens in nearly every single scene that Layne and Rocky are together...I'm not even exaggerating. And get this: she never wins!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383404416i/6543368.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>-- The parenting portrayed here? WTF was that?!?! Bullshit, that's what.</i>
</b><br>Who not only lets, but recruits their 17 and 14 year old children to infiltrate a known pedophile's operation? <br><br><b>
  <i>-- The ex situation: Tanner Layne's ex wife and loving mother of his children was portrayed as such a bitch. </i>
</b> And I'm sorry, but if the father of my children encouraged profanity, utilized them in his oh-so-manly, deadly sting operations, and encouraged their promiscuity (not by offering condoms...to each his own. I'm talking about the joking and subtle pseudo high fives and the fact that <b>Layne alludes to the way that Keira, Joe Cal's daughter, is somehow more DESERVING of respect with regards to sex and affection than the other girls he was banging...this pissed me off. No one is less deserving of respect, especially gullible teenage girls.</b>), not to mention the fact that he basically took off for nearly their entire lives and suddenly wants to come back and tell her how to raise them. And SHE'S the bitch? Nope, not even close.<br><br>My last point of contention was the big conflict. This is a second chance love story. Twenty years or so have passed since Rocky left their happy relationship out of the blue, suddenly and with no explanation. The build up to that big revelation took nearly this entire book. Her dad and her brother were both in on it, adamant that Rocky would never speak to them again if they revealed the big secret. And after the revelation, I mean <b>what revelation?</b> I still don't see any reasoning behind her actions. I mean, seriously, what a lame, lazy excuse. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She left because her mom died when she was ten and she had to listen to her die,felt guilty for not stepping in, and started her period and couldn't talk to her brother and Dad about it? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Soooooo...what? That means she can never have a meaningful relationship? That means she should leave the love of her life, with zero explanation? Here one day, gone the next. For me, there WAS NO REASON given. None. It was sort of glossed over. All we really get is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Rocky having some kind of mental breakdown <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>There are a few epic quotes in these pages and I can absolutely see the appeal for fans of KA to love this. (Here I go again...evade, evade, evade...) I think for me, it was a combination of really bad timing and the fact that not only did I start to lose interest early on in the book, but that this is also one of the 500+ monsters of earlier KA. I honestly hate to rip apart this book like I did, but I'm being honest and I just couldn't find any redeeming qualities for this story. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394122455i/8811136.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Wait...on second thought, since Rocky was such a doormat, maybe she really and truly needed an uber bossy man to make decisions for her. That could actually be the entire point of the story, and instead of embracing it, I just now thought of it at the end of my review. Dang.<br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3415445804804033303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_407886755" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/407886755" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/407886755?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer407886755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16309499714934934736"><i> <b> "Live this with me, just live it, whatever happens, however it happens, just live it with me..." </b> </i><br/><br/><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390204i/751800._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>**HAPPY DANCE** oooo how I loved this book! It literally made me tremble with joy (yes, literally... and my husband is still teasing me about my incessant squeeing :P ). But seriously, its another gorgeous, swoony, emotional beautifully written KA book that had me in happy tears and clutching my heart more times than I could count. <br/><br/>Tanner Layne wakes up in a hospital bed after being riddled with b</span>
  <span id="freeText16309499714934934736" style="display:none"><i> <b> "Live this with me, just live it, whatever happens, however it happens, just live it with me..." </b> </i><br><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390204i/751800._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>**HAPPY DANCE** oooo how I loved this book! It literally made me tremble with joy (yes, literally... and my husband is still teasing me about my incessant squeeing :P ). But seriously, its another gorgeous, swoony, emotional beautifully written KA book that had me in happy tears and clutching my heart more times than I could count. <br><br>Tanner Layne wakes up in a hospital bed after being riddled with bullets to find Rocky at his bed side. To say their history was a mess is an understatement. 18 years ago, they had a beautiful, know-in-your-heart-this-is-meant-to-be-forever kind of romance until suddenly, with no reason, Rocky left him. Devastated and unable to find the reason why, Layne left the 'burg and moved forward with his life while leaving his heart behind. Heart broken and angry over Rocky's unexplained departure from his life, his condom breaks one very drunk night giving him a son he adores but saddling him with a bitchy wife he feels duty bound to stand by. Trapped for years in a loveless marriage, the only good thing left in his life becomes his two sons. Now, in present day, his ex-wife has hooked up with a real asshole he doesn't want around his two teenage sons, and he has come back to the 'burg in an effort to give them a better life. But when he wakes up in the hospital and sees Rocky there for him, and then they start working together to bring down the dirty cop who shot him, it reawakens his feelings for her that were buried so deep by the hurt of their past that he didn't realize how truly strong they still were.<br><br><b> <i> Layne knew he was in love with her. Not only that, he'd never stopped loving her. Not once, not for a second, not for twenty-one years.<br>Fuck him. </i> </b><br><br>The whole vibe of this book is a little different than the last two in the series (For You and At Peace). It really snuck up on me because while it seemed a lot quieter and more subtle in its intensity, it packed quite the emotional punch. I cried several times (usually happy or just overly emotional tears), squeed, laughed, swooned and really just felt a lot while reading it. Something about it really spoke deep. Deep family connections, deep bonding, deep love and healing. Just. So. Freaking. Gorgeous.<br><br>And while there is still very much of the typical 'badass' feel that all KA books have, it has that while being very strongly family-relationship focused. It felt very real. There is a lot of family stuff that is just utterly gorgeous and because Layne has two sons (the oldest being 18), its basically a badass KA Alpha man raising KA Alpha boys - total mega swoon going on there!! I cannot possibly tell you guys how much I ADORED seeing Layne and his sons bond. Definitely led to a lot of tears and heart clutching &lt;3<br><br>Another thing that's different is that the whole book is from Layne's POV! I loved seeing the life, thoughts and actions of a KA Alpha man so continuously. By always seeing the story from his POV, you totally sympathized with his lack of knowledge about the break up and were just as curious as he was to uncover the reason behind it, and you saw him fall back in love with Rocky and got to see the romance build through his eyes.<br><br>The romantic relationship part of this story is a slow, subtle but beautiful build. Its not like they see each other and the clothing articles go a-flyin'. The romance creeps up on them as they slowly and naturally ease back into the "forever" couple they were always intended to be while working out the issues left over by so many unanswered questions. *dreamy sigh* ... oh, and the sexy times were HOT!! <i> "Hands to the wall." </i> *fans self*<br><br>There IS a bad guy, but, unlike in previous books in this series, he isn't really directly targeting Layne or Rocky, but rather actually serves to being them closer to each other as they work together to bring him down.<br><br>And then there is the whole issue of Rocky's big secret - why did she leave Layne 18 years ago?? We don't find out until late in the story - the build up is subtle but intense! As the theories started piling up in my head, I was on emotional overload. Full body chills, tears, the whole shebang!<br><br>I loved watching them come together, watching Rocky open up to him again, watching him making her feel safe, and seeing them meld their lives back together.<br><br><b> "I remember, Rocky. I remember everything. I remember every... <i> fucking </i> ... thing." </b><br><br>Layne was such a gorgeous Alpha. But he was open, honest, fair, loyal, no bullshit, no lies, no games. Just seeing him pass on his wisdom and teaching his sons to be the best men they could be both through his words and by practicing what he was preaching and always being there for his woman, respecting her, loving her, protecting her... helping those in need, bringing his family together... absolutely beautiful, totally swoony, and heart-melting!! &lt;3<br><br><i> "Seen a lot of things, done a lot of things, wounds to the flesh hurt but they heal fast. Wounds to the soul never go away. It's how we cope with a pain that never dies that makes us the people we are. Daily, people demonstrate acts of courage just so they can get through the night.. there are warriors and then there are warriors. In your Dad's bed lies a warrior. Learn from her, boy." </i><br><br>Rocky was a wonderful heroine. She had guts, was strong on her own, stubborn and driven. She drove Layne a little crazy sometimes with how strong she was, but that was great fun to read cuz it brought out his swoony extra protective side. But she also had a lot of buried hurt, a lot of deep understanding for love and a beautiful heart. She was the perfect match for Layne.<br><br>There were so many times in the story when I'd just be sitting there reading with tears in my eyes and my hand over my mouth... beautiful, emotional, deep. Love, love, love!<br><br>The story also ties into the previous two books in the series. We see a lot of Colt &amp; Feb and Cal &amp; Vi and their girls... them all living in the 'burg together and all being in the business of protecting people, their lives intersect a lot. And its totally awesome!<br><br>I know I've said this a few gazillion times before, but seriously. KA writes THE. BEST. MEN. EVER. (who am I kidding, she writes pretty much the best EVERYTHING ever, but I digress). My heart just overflows with the emotions that their stories and actions wring from me and their stories settle so deeply in my heart, I feel like I know these characters personal. Utterly BRILLIANT writing. That woman has a true gift. Her writing style is just so badass. She makes absolutely everything seem larger than life and epically cool and yet so down-to-earth, real and intimate that it feels like its just you and the world you are reading about and you can just lose yourself in the words and feel like you are right freaking there.<br><br>Oh, and there is a GORGEOUS epilogue at the end of this book featuring all the characters we've seen in this series so far... KA's epilogues leave you with the most wonderful, happy, full feelings ever. They leave you with the knowledge and deep certainty that everyone in them has the beautiful happy ending they deserve. *happy tear*<br><br>Here's how I see Layne: <img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390204i/751801._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Aestas Book Blog</a><br><br>And come join the Aestas Book Blog <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener"> Facebook Page</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16309499714934934736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Georgia ♥ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9138738-georgia"><img alt="Georgia ♥ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377186210p2/9138738.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/492801145?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Georgia ♥ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Georgia ♥ " href="/user/show/9138738-georgia">Georgia ♥ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9138738-georgia?shelf=adorable-baby-toddler-kid-teenager">adorable-baby-toddler-kid-teenager</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9138738-georgia?shelf=the-sound-of-my-heart-breaking">the-sound-of-my-heart-breaking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9138738-georgia?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9138738-georgia?shelf=lol-chuckle-worthy">lol-chuckle-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9138738-georgia?shelf=sobbing-mess">sobbing-mess</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer492801145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15974397929458492409"><b>5 Kristen Ashley Stars!</b> (Kristen Ashley = amazing)<br/><br/><i>Just when I thought I've seen it all and there was no way I'd enjoy a book about long separated lovers and teenaged boys, Kristen Ashley turned the tables on me, moved for the win and FRAKKING did it again!!!!!<br/><br/><b>Ladies fasten your seatbelts, and prepare yourselves... We are inside the mind of Tanner Layne, alpha male extraordinaire!!!!!!!!!!!!</b></i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380403144i/784211.png' width='500' height='295' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Entirely told in his POV, this book surprises you, captivates you and gives you a rare glimpse at the amazi</span>
  <span id="freeText15974397929458492409" style="display:none"><b>5 Kristen Ashley Stars!</b> (Kristen Ashley = amazing)<br><br><i>Just when I thought I've seen it all and there was no way I'd enjoy a book about long separated lovers and teenaged boys, Kristen Ashley turned the tables on me, moved for the win and FRAKKING did it again!!!!!<br><br><b>Ladies fasten your seatbelts, and prepare yourselves... We are inside the mind of Tanner Layne, alpha male extraordinaire!!!!!!!!!!!!</b></i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380403144i/784211.png" width="500" height="295" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Entirely told in his POV, this book surprises you, captivates you and gives you a rare glimpse at the amazing psyche of our favorite heroes, KA males!! I mean it's a new species, really...<br><br><i>
  <b>“Any battle worth winnin’ is worth using every weapon available.” </b>
</i><br><br>Every time, every damn time these books make me live, love, FEEL.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380366373ra/718578.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b> “I was a child, and she was a child, in this kingdom by the sea; but we loved with a love that was more than a love – I and my Annabelle Lee.” </b>
</i><br><br>Layne and Rocky fell in love young. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380402814ra/783221.gif" width="500" height="290" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And they had it all.<br><br><i>
  <b> “You were my first kiss, my first everything. ”</b>
</i><br><br>But they also had demons. Nightmares to fight and Raquel Merrick was many things but she wasn't well. She was strong beyond your wild imaginings, but not sane.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>
    <b> “I left you to give you a life, baby,” she whispered, her voice hoarse, the tears hitting her eyes, sliding down, silent. “I wanted you to have a life.”</b>
  </i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And she left. And they were broken.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403144ra/784212.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Eighteen years later. They tried. They tried to built a life. <br><br>Layne tried to built a family, but his wife wasn't Rocky. She was a bitch. He has two teenaged sons, he is a P.I and he tries to save everyone. In his line of work he is injured and laying in hospital he wakes up (in more ways than one) with Rocky by his side.<br><br>Rocky tried too. She married, but her husband wasn't Layne. He was a cheating bastard. Humiliated and lonely, her only salvation are her students and her passion in her work. She is the most popular English Lit teacher. Hell, the most beloved teacher. She once left Layne and she knows she might do it again. But his getting shot, is a wake up call and she can't resist him a second time.<br><br>Two people, scarred and miserable alone, realise that they can leave the past behind and that noone has to be perfect. They just have to be themselves.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380401264ra/778580.gif" width="500" height="271" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And in the end:<br><i>
  <b>“If you’re nothing else in this life, be wise, be compassionate and be strong because those three things are everything.” </b>
</i><br><br>Amazing secondary characters as always with KA novels. Tripp and Jasper are awesome. Mature, responsible, mini-Layne delights. OK, I'm not 100% sure about their involvement with the case but hell, I liked it! I wouldn't want my kids a mile within this, but for this story it totally worked! And the Jasper-Keira romance it was a treat! I LOVED it.<br>The whole brilliant 'Burg cast is here and they have closed ranks more than ever. Don't mess with them people!!!<br><br>The Epilogue was the cherry on top of this fantastic cake.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/396381.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/466989.gif" width="300" height="169" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>THANK YOU! THANK YOU! A MILLION TIMES THANK YOU KRISTEN! You always deliver....</b><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1179861002" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1179861002" />
    <a title="Flo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7643503-flo"><img alt="Flo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597575025p2/7643503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1179861002?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flo" href="/user/show/7643503-flo">Flo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7643503-flo?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7643503-flo?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7643503-flo?shelf=best-of-2015">best-of-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7643503-flo?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1179861002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5390487439201101354"><b>5 excuse me while I swoon a little STARS</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422275130i/13479350.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Men like you aren’t made, though, Tanner. Men like you just are. ”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>LADIES! We got a bad-ass alpha male DILF on our hands. I'm a believer in sharing good new first and this is the best news ever, believe me. And the whole book is written in his POV...what more do you want?<br/><br/>Honestly? This stuff is just perfect which ever way you look at it. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2958084.Kristen_Ashley' title='Kristen Ashley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kristen Ashley</a> books are like my safe haven. I come back to them with alarming frequency and once I start I </span>
  <span id="freeText5390487439201101354" style="display:none"><b>5 excuse me while I swoon a little STARS</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422275130i/13479350.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Men like you aren’t made, though, Tanner. Men like you just are. ”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>LADIES! We got a bad-ass alpha male DILF on our hands. I'm a believer in sharing good new first and this is the best news ever, believe me. And the whole book is written in his POV...what more do you want?<br><br>Honestly? This stuff is just perfect which ever way you look at it. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2958084.Kristen_Ashley" title="Kristen Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristen Ashley</a> books are like my safe haven. I come back to them with alarming frequency and once I start I can never stop. I said this before, but <i>for me</i> escaping into one of her books is like eating comfort food and just coming home.<br>It's wonderful.<br><br>Now I'm not going to lie, KA writes these books with an painting by numbers approach. You know what you get and I'm totally ok with that every once in a while, it's also the thing that makes it so easy to read. A bit of predictability and some heart warming cheesy fluff, mixed in with a little mystery, murder and mayhem. No regrets here. She gets me every time.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418911509i/12944326.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“If you are nothing else in this life, be wise, be compassionate, and be strong because those three are everything.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Tanner Layne</b> was shot during an investigation into a corrupt cop and when he wakes up at the hospital he is greeted with a face he didn't expect, not in a million years. <b>Raquel 'Rocky' Merrick</b>.<br><br>Rocky and Layne have a very intense history, but for the last eighteen years they haven't even talked to one another. When Roc was 17 and Layne was 21 they started dating for three years until one day Rocky left....out of the blue and with no explanation whatsoever. In fact she enlisted her father and brother to keep him from her.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/604796.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And Layne was forced to move on from the only woman he had ever loved. Shortly after a drunken hook up resulted in a failed marriage and two sons; Jasper, 17 and Tripp, 14. Eighteen years after the break-up that almost destroyed him he is not only a devoted father who not always makes the right decisions, but tries like no one else; but also a hard working and very successful Private Investigator.<br><br>Rocky on the other hand had moved on as well, she is a teacher now and she got married eventually. Unfortunately her ass-hole husband cheated on her and she left him. Not that she was very heartbroken about it since that relationship was just as loveless as Layne's was.<br><br>Roc is a wonderful character. I really liked her a lot. She is sweet, caring, a brilliant teacher and just through and through a good person. Which makes the fact that she left him before all the more unbelievable and the actual reason so much more painful.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418911509i/12944326.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Layne knew he was in love with her. Not only that, he’d never stopped loving her. Not once, not for a second, not for twenty-one years.<br>Fuck him.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>After Layne got shot something within Roc shifted and she couldn't stay away any longer. Hence the wake-up call in the hospital room. And she goes even further, Rocky is out for revenge. She wants to get the SOBs who did this to Jayne, but also she has history with dirty cops and she just doesn't stand for that kind of behaviour. Ultimately things get set in motion that forces them to to work together.<br><br>And to be honest, deep down both just want an excuse to be near one another again. Of course they can't stay away for long and with a bit of strategic manoeuvring on Layne's part things get really interesting pretty darn fast.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422387803i/13496981.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now you just have to throw a few more people into the mix - KA style. Layne's two teenage sons who make some pretty awesome mini-alphas in training, his grumpy old CIA friend Dev, his mother, the dog named Blondie and then there is the scary biker with the big heart named Ryker. That's just the inner circle. There is so much more going on, at times I wanted to draw a flow chart just to keep up with all the cases our hero was working on.<br><br>You see, Layne has a bit of a helper complex and he can't say no to people in need. It's adorable and pretty bad-ass as well. So on top of finding out who shot him, there are many many more riddles to solve and lives to save.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418911509i/12944326.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Wounds to the flesh hurt but they heal fast. Wounds to the soul never go away. It’s how we cope with a pain that never dies that makes us the people we are. Daily, people demonstrate acts of courage just so they can get through to the night”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><i>Golden Trail</i> is one of those books you either love to pieces or you just can't deal with. It's long...and I mean looooong. Over 700 pages long. But here is the kicker, I would have read a few hundred more without thinking about it. I love Ms. Ashley's style. I love her attention to detail and I freaking adore this world she created where the protagonists from previous books in the series play big roles as well.<br><br>Over the span of now three books in this particular series (plus two more I haven't read yet) we get to explore the 'burg and all its inhabitants, the criminal proceedings and the tragedies that lie just beneath the surface. But it all leads to happy endings, lots of love and family. The sense of community and help between the people is just heart-warming.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“His fingers curled around her neck and he put his forehead to hers before sharing, “I remember, Rocky. I remember everything. I remember every… fucking… thing.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>So, we have my personal holy grail of romance tropes - a beautiful second chance love-story. I'm always ok with that. A male POV told story and let me tell you this is one testosterone filled read. Not only is our MC a no bullshit, take no prisoners hard ass, he also tells it like he means it. I don't think he even knows how to lie. His interaction with his sons it really well done. He treats them like adults and actually considers them as assets. Then you have all the other boys running around, helping out and investigating stuff. It's all manly talk and 'you got me?' shit. I freaking loved it!!!<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418911509i/12944326.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://coffeeaddictbooks.blogspot.co.at/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431601625i/14852808.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/coffeeaddictbooks?ref=tn_tnmn" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431598100i/14852514.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://twitter.com/flo_reads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431598236i/14852521.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="http://coffeeaddictbooks.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431598236i/14852522.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/101016591301224002138" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431598236i/14852523.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<span id="freeTextContainer261760015566331771">Re read - upgraded from 4-5 stars!<br/><br/>I loved this book the first time around!<br/><br/>I loved it even more the second time around.<br/><br/>Tanner and Rocky had been in love 18 years ago - until Rocky left with no warning and refused to talk to Tanner about it, or speak to Tanner ever again.<br/><br/>At the beginning of the story, Tanner who is now a divorced PI with 2 teen sons, had been shot while working a case, and Rocky could not keep away.<br/><br/>This story is told entirely in Tanner's POV, and here it worked! <br/><br/>He was going in Bl</span>
  <span id="freeText261760015566331771" style="display:none">Re read - upgraded from 4-5 stars!<br /><br />I loved this book the first time around!<br /><br />I loved it even more the second time around.<br /><br />Tanner and Rocky had been in love 18 years ago - until Rocky left with no warning and refused to talk to Tanner about it, or speak to Tanner ever again.<br /><br />At the beginning of the story, Tanner who is now a divorced PI with 2 teen sons, had been shot while working a case, and Rocky could not keep away.<br /><br />This story is told entirely in Tanner's POV, and here it worked! <br /><br />He was going in Blind, into a relationship with Rocky again, not knowing what had driven her away, not knowing how to navigate the minefield that was getting back to them being a couple again, and we were walking that path with him. <br /><br />We knew his heartbreak, we knew his love, we knew his regrets, we knew his hope and we knew his fear that it would all happen again and he would be left alone!<br /><br />Tanner Layne, he is a man who made mistakes, and has paid for them, but he is a beautiful beautiful man, trying to do his best now and have his love.<br /><br />It is very cleverly written, you can feel it building, knowing something is going to happen, and Rocky is beginning to feel what it was that made her leave years ago. <br /><br />There is a lot going on in this book, with regards to what Tanner is working on, and on the first read, this was fine, but on the second read, I found it a lot easier to keep track of and connect all the dots.<br /><br />And it goes without saying, as with every KA book, an excellent set of secondary characters, who you care about and love.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1387782289" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1387782289?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=guilty-pleasure-read">guilty-pleasure-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=3-stars-aint-the-devil">3-stars-aint-the-devil</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=i-wouldnt-tell-my-mama-i-read-this">i-wouldnt-tell-my-mama-i-read-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=kristen-ashley-aka-the-queen">kristen-ashley-aka-the-queen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1387782289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12357886589202452417"><b> 3 stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “If you are nothing else in this life, be wise, be compassionate, and be strong because those three are everything." </i> </b><br/><br/>The Burg series seems to be a hit or miss for me. I never made it through the first book, the second book was amazing, and this one I liked but didn't love.<br/><br/>Golden Trail is the story of Tanner Layne and Raquel 'Rocky' Merrick. The two were in love at a very young age until Rocky left Layne with no explanation and left him broken hearted. Fast forward eighteen years and</span>
  <span id="freeText12357886589202452417" style="display:none"><b> 3 stars! </b><br /><br /><b> <i> “If you are nothing else in this life, be wise, be compassionate, and be strong because those three are everything." </i> </b><br /><br />The Burg series seems to be a hit or miss for me. I never made it through the first book, the second book was amazing, and this one I liked but didn't love.<br /><br />Golden Trail is the story of Tanner Layne and Raquel 'Rocky' Merrick. The two were in love at a very young age until Rocky left Layne with no explanation and left him broken hearted. Fast forward eighteen years and Rocky wants to help Layne on a case, so the two pretend being a couple. Very soon pretend becomes real and Layne is left worrying if Rocky will leave him again.<br /><br /><b> <i> “Layne knew he was in love with her. Not only that, he’d never stopped loving her. Not once, not for a second, not for twenty-one years.<br />Fuck him.” </i> </b><br /><br />There's not much to say, three star reads are the hardest for me to write because while I liked it, I didn't love. It's an average book. I found the POV of Layne only to be interesting but I would have liked something from Rocky. And after 18 years apart them getting back together seemed a bit anti-climactic for me.<br /><br />I would have loved this book but plot wise it was all over the damn place and it was jarring. Plus it was waaaayyyyyyy too long. Some great emotional parts, but Kristen Ashley has done better *cough cough* Play It Safe was the same story with less time gap and done better *cough cough*<br /><br />I still love The Queen of Romance Miss KA! Onward!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12357886589202452417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_268030813" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/268030813" />
    <a title="Shawna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1802746-shawna"><img alt="Shawna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574172018p2/1802746.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/268030813?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawna" href="/user/show/1802746-shawna">Shawna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of KA, second chance romances, &amp; protective alpha heroes</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=format-ebook">format-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=small-town-lovin-small-town-setting">small-town-lovin-small-town-setting</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-brooding">hero-brooding</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=villain-uber-bad-nasty">villain-uber-bad-nasty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-alpha%E2%80%8E">hero-alpha‎</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=cheating-fidelityissues-past-or-new">cheating-fidelityissues-past-or-new</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer268030813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5421917029065827385">4 ½-5 stars – Contemporary Romance/Romantic Suspense<br/><br/>Another Kristen Ashley winner! Do I even need to say anything more than that? Probably not, so instead of a typical review, I’m going to do some general rambling.<br/><br/><u>What I Loved</u>:<br/><br/>#1 -- It’s told entirely from the hero’s POV, which is A+wesome!<br/> <br/>That brings me to item #2, which is the hero, Tanner Layne. He’s a badass PI, a tough alpha male, and a devoted lover and father struggling to reconcile with his past, one and only, true love and make amends </span>
  <span id="freeText5421917029065827385" style="display:none">4 ½-5 stars – Contemporary Romance/Romantic Suspense<br><br>Another Kristen Ashley winner! Do I even need to say anything more than that? Probably not, so instead of a typical review, I’m going to do some general rambling.<br><br><u>What I Loved</u>:<br><br>#1 -- It’s told entirely from the hero’s POV, which is A+wesome!<br> <br>That brings me to item #2, which is the hero, Tanner Layne. He’s a badass PI, a tough alpha male, and a devoted lover and father struggling to reconcile with his past, one and only, true love and make amends with his teen boys while also trying to teach them how to be men.<br><br>And this takes me to favorite things about the book #3 and #4 -- Layne’s teen sons, Jasper and Tripp. They’re KA heartthrobs and heroes in their own right and made me feel a little bit dirty and cougar-ish for seriously crushing on teenagers. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jasper and Keira and Trip and Giselle seemed to get their own HEAs, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>but I really hope we haven’t seen the last of them. In fact, I’d love for Jasper and Tripp to be featured as main (legal and guilt free) heroes in future KA books. LOL!<br><br>#5 -- A great secondary cast of characters, especially mysterious badass, Ryker. I’m also looking forward to Garrett Merrick’s story.<br><br>#6 -- The <i>To Kill a Mockingbird</i> reference and how it’s an allegory for the story.<br><br>#7 -- The sweet and gratifying epilogue that’s worthy of 10+ stars!<br><br><u>Wacky But Whatever, It Still Worked Somehow</u>:<br><br>Parenting 101 -- I’m not a parent so I can’t rightfully judge someone’s child rearing skills, but that doesn’t mean I can’t shake my head a few times with a seriously?, huh?, or wtf? There were several characters (Layne, Gabby, Vera, Dave, etc.) who demonstrated questionable parenting. I’m honestly not sure how I feel about some of Layne’s parenting decisions and actions, like involving his teenage sons, ages 14 and 17, in an undercover operation of a shady youth group. I imagine he would probably raise the eyebrows of some parental experts. But raising teenagers to be compassionate, responsible adults who do the right thing isn’t easy. I liked his honesty and that he didn’t shield Jasper and Tripp from the harsh realities of life. And it seemed to all work out for the best.<br><br>Talk Show Worthy Family Drama -- I think several characters in this book needed some counseling. Seriously, Dr. Phil would have a freakin field day with these people.<br><br>Crazy Exes, Multiple Plots, and Uber Villains -- Layne’s b*tchy ex-wife Gabby and her loser, enforcer boyfriend, Rocky’s cheating doctor ex and his shady financial and business dealings, and an undercover investigation of a sinister youth minister <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[whose group is really a front for recruiting girls for a child pornography, underage sexual slavery/prostitution ring <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> run by a female mastermind villain who makes Cruella de Vil look like the Easter Bunny.<br> <br>The Big Secret Reveal -- It was a heartbreaking scene, but also seemed very melodramatic and overly angsty.<br><br><u>Petty Grievances</u>:<br><br>The Hero’s Name -- Layne is a nerdy programmer analyst with fancy pencils in his pocket and Tanner is a badass biker or cowboy (and <i>Days of Our Lives</i> soap opera bad boy from the early 90’s). So I would have preferred that the hero went by his first name, Tanner, instead of his last name, Layne.<br><br>The Heroine’s Name –- She has a beautiful name, Raquel, but everyone calls her Rocky?! Ugh!<br><br>Size Matters -- KA’s stories are characteristically detailed and lengthy, but this one felt <i>looong</i>. I think it could have used some trimming down.<br><br>But despite all the wackiness and some imperfections, I <i>loved</i> it! Nearly 5 stars!<br><br>Layne<br><a href="http://s1206.photobucket.com/albums/bb447/shawnarazz/?action=view&amp;current=11331751_ori.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368328i/720888.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Jasper (Now you can understand why I was crushing hard on a teenager!)<br><a href="http://s1206.photobucket.com/albums/bb447/shawnarazz/?action=view&amp;current=500full.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368328i/720889.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Tripp <br><a href="http://s1206.photobucket.com/albums/bb447/shawnarazz/?action=view&amp;current=112331_logan-lerman-promotes-percy-jackson-and-the-olympians-the-lightning-thief-at-borders-kips-bay-on-feb.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368328i/720890.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
