<div id="review_251856529" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/251856529" />
    <a title="KatLynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2435483-katlynne"><img alt="KatLynne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296698899p2/2435483.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/251856529?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KatLynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KatLynne" href="/user/show/2435483-katlynne">KatLynne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=hero-favorite-smokin-hot-sexay">hero-favorite-smokin-hot-sexay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=heroine-tormented-flawed">heroine-tormented-flawed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=one-of-my-favorite-series">one-of-my-favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=favorite-treasures">favorite-treasures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=small-town-livin">small-town-livin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=keeper">keeper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=g-romantic-suspense">g-romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251856529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13849816006511346903"><b> 4.5 Stars and Another winner by KA!</b><br/><br/><i> "I was a child, and she was a child, in this kingdom by the sea; but we loved with a love that was more than a love - I and my Annabelle Lee. But our love was stronger by far than the love of those much older than we, of many far wiser than we, and neither the angels in heaven above, nor the demons down under the sea, can ever dissever my soul from the soul of the beautiful Annabelle Lee.” (Poe’s Annabelle Lee) </i><br/><br/>I believe this may be my first read from the her</span>
  <span id="freeText13849816006511346903" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 Stars and Another winner by KA!</b><br /><br /><i> "I was a child, and she was a child, in this kingdom by the sea; but we loved with a love that was more than a love - I and my Annabelle Lee. But our love was stronger by far than the love of those much older than we, of many far wiser than we, and neither the angels in heaven above, nor the demons down under the sea, can ever dissever my soul from the soul of the beautiful Annabelle Lee.” (Poe’s Annabelle Lee) </i><br /><br />I believe this may be my first read from the hero’s point-of-view and it did not disappoint!<br /><br />What can I say that hasn’t been said about KA’s books?! This is another great read with an amazing hero and heroine who are both gorgeous, sassy and smart, loveable secondary characters and included are those wonderful visits with old friends from previous books. And as always, we are introduced to new characters that stole my heart and a fabulous epilogue! <br /> <br />Similar to the first story in this series, Tanner Layne, hot, sexy PI and Raquel “Rocky” Merrick have been apart for eighteen years! Back in the day, twenty year old Rocky, without rhyme or reason, walked out on twenty four year old Layne. Refusing to see him or speak with him, he is broken. She’d “torn out his heart and shattered his world.” On a drunken binge, a night of sex soon turns into pregnancy and a marriage to a woman he doesn’t love. A few years into this marriage, Layne realizes it must end when the news of a second child is on the way. But even with two young boys, this marriage was doomed and ends in divorce.<br /><br />Now, Layne is back home for the first time in over twelve years! He has moved back to the 'Burg' in order to be more pro-active in the lives of his two teenage sons. He and Rocky manage to avoid each other, but soon after taking three bullets while investigating a local dirty cop, this changes. <br /><br />Throughout the book I kept wondering why Rocky had left Layne. It’s very evident they had a deep love and had planned to spend a life together. It just didn’t make sense. Eighteen years apart! But this beautiful, smart woman has suffered and when the agonies of her suffering are revealed, it is brutally heart wrenching and I felt her pain! Witnessing this and finally knowing why she left, Tanner Layne does what KA’s heroes are famous for; he wraps his woman with tenderness, love and intense possessive protection. <br /><br />I don’t think there was anything I didn’t like about this story other than the many years they were apart! It is filled with one crime after another. There also is the family drama that always seems so real, along with the asswipes that you despise and of course the hot, steamy love scenes. <br /><br />An added bonus for me was the reference made to one of my favorite classics, To Kill A Mockingbird! Rocky’s words describing Atticus Finch reveals much of Tanner Layne’s character….<br /> <i> “Atticus Finch is the most beautiful man I’ve ever met in print. He’s a good dad and he does what’s right, not what’s safe, not what’s popular. What’s right. He’s gentle. He’s smart. He’s strong. He’s decisive and he’s willing to follow through with his decisions, no matter what the odds.” </i><br /><br />When you add these attributes to a gorgeous, sexy, dangerous man, who can resist? <br /><br />Rocky is easily one of my favorite heroines! I could go on and on but I think this quote says it all….<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Wounds to the flesh hurt, but they heal fast. Wounds to the soul never go away. It’s how we cope with a pain that never dies that makes us the people we are. …That woman upstairs smiles and laughs and cooks and teaches and no one knew the pain she carried in her soul. In other words, there are warriors and then there are warriors. In your Dad’s bed lies a warrior. Learn from her.”  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This is one of the best second chance at love books I’ve read and easily a favorite and a keeper! KA’s mix is a winner for me every time. This entire series has been great and I’m anxiously looking forward to more!<br /><br />I liked Rocky's thoughts on books and thought I'd share:)<br /><b> That’s the beauty of books. We get to take what we want out of them and it can be different for everyone.”</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13849816006511346903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2091628164" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2091628164" />
    <a title="fleurette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4692637-fleurette"><img alt="fleurette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357165343p2/4692637.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2091628164?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="fleurette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="fleurette" href="/user/show/4692637-fleurette">fleurette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24922662-golden-trail">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4692637-fleurette?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4692637-fleurette?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2091628164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8723339189439893944">This was my first book by Kristen Ashley. I know people love her and her books but this one just didn't work for me. It wasn't really awful but it wasn't worth my time at this moment.<br/><br/>Let's make it clear, it is a really well-written book and despite its length it is somehow easy to read. It wasn't sooo long I would probably finish it. But unfortunately it is really long and I gave up at 30% and read only the ending. So, these are my thoughts about one third of the book. And there are also so many</span>
  <span id="freeText8723339189439893944" style="display:none">This was my first book by Kristen Ashley. I know people love her and her books but this one just didn't work for me. It wasn't really awful but it wasn't worth my time at this moment.<br /><br />Let's make it clear, it is a really well-written book and despite its length it is somehow easy to read. It wasn't sooo long I would probably finish it. But unfortunately it is really long and I gave up at 30% and read only the ending. So, these are my thoughts about one third of the book. And there are also so many things I didn't actually like.<br /><br />First, I know people have some problems with Layne, I didn't and I think it is because I was constantly annoyed with Rocky. She comes to Layne house after about twenty years, and she doesn't explain what for. Then she advises him on housekeeping and parenting. What a bitch! And since she is an English literature teacher she decides that she will investigate a case of a dirty cop. The one who killed her mother, nearly killed her father who is a policeman, and just shot one of the very best PIs. But she is sooo capable of catching him. And because she is a teacher and her brother and father are policemen and her false lover a PI, she decides she has to investigate another potentially dangerous case that involves breaking into a church at midnight. Go get them, girl! She is a weak heroine and I couldn't get attached to her. Layne didn't annoy me as much, except for the fact that he finds Rocky <i>*cute*</i> (a grown-up woman! like a puppy or a newborn!). <br /><br />Another thing that I really hated about this book are the dialogues. Three fourth of them are Rocky talking and Layne just repeating her name umpteen times or him talking and her repeating. <br /><br /><blockquote>But she just called and said she’s going to be late and I can’t miss this viewing because if I do someone else might snatch up the apartment –”<br />“Rocky –”<br />“And I gotta get off –”<br />“Roc –”<br />“Merry’s couch or my back is going to –”<br />“Sweetcheeks, shut up a second,” he cut in...</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>“Rocky, what’d I tell you about this shit?” he asked.<br />“Layne –”<br />“Put the file back and get your ass to your car.”<br />“Layne –”</blockquote><br /><br />This is the miscommunication level master. I couldn’t stand it, I was rolling my eyes time after time. More than half of the drama in this book could be avoided if only the MC talked to each other like two adult human beings. <br /><br />Also, the book is long. But it is long not because of the very developed plot, though there are many sub-plots, too many in my opinion. No, it is long because of all those drawn-out descriptions, meaningless conversations and completely unnecessary insights into the characters' thoughts. Don't get me wrong, I like to know my characters and have them developed, but, really, I don't care if Layne likes the coach he is sitting on or the view from the window, definitely not to read the whole paragraph about his opinions. And the action is so slow that you can skip like fifty pages and you will be in the same place. The suspense part is just not moving a jot. The thing is that we know more about the types of trees growing in front of Rocky's flat than about the scheme she and Layne are into. And then we've got umpteen other sub-plots that add up to the whole unnecessary drama. [I read some reviews and people say that the suspense part is actually good. I can't tall about that after reading only one third of the story.] <br /><br />I didn't really dislike this book. The point is that I didn't really care. As I said if it wasn't so long I would probably read the whole thing. Especially that I really liked Jasper and Tripp. I will probably give this author another chance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8723339189439893944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251421387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14255253761158194982"> <b>5***** Stars THE HERO'S STORY</b> This entire story was told in the first person by the HERO!! That's so cool. Out of the 700 + romance books that I have read, not once was the entire story told by the hero. That is soooo friggin cool. Gabaldon does that a little in her books, but NOT THE WHOLE STORY! It was a great story and long. And that's cool too because I also friggin love looooong. Books, that is. (hehe) Okay so I'm doing the happy dance. I'll try to control myself. Great story, great charac</span>
  <span id="freeText14255253761158194982" style="display:none"> <b>5***** Stars THE HERO'S STORY</b> This entire story was told in the first person by the HERO!! That's so cool. Out of the 700 + romance books that I have read, not once was the entire story told by the hero. That is soooo friggin cool. Gabaldon does that a little in her books, but NOT THE WHOLE STORY! It was a great story and long. And that's cool too because I also friggin love looooong. Books, that is. (hehe) Okay so I'm doing the happy dance. I'll try to control myself. Great story, great characters. Again. And Oh My God Layne! Did you get that.<br />Oh.<br />My.<br />God.<br />Layne.<br />He is the coolest dad, PI dude, friend, and lover. Kristen Ashley has nailed and I mean nailed the Alpha dream man in her books. If you haven't read a Kristen Ashley book you need to get started ASAP. I would suggest "Sweet Dreams" this being my favorite. I loved this one too, but the secondary characters in "Sweet Dreams" were so awesome that I don't think they can be beat. This story was just as awesome and recommend it because of it being told by the hero, which I think should not be missed. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer431355515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8129824932698661286">3.5 to 4 stars... As other reviewers have said, this was different than any KA. It was told from the male lead perspective and I think there were a lot of missed opportunities (the Jasper/Keira storyline could have been a lot more IMO) but it was still a KA and very entertaining. Sometimes I felt like there were too many "cases" going on at once, but it's that over the top action that makes her books fun.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GSku1fcRVWLf50eSAQiXEvk4ksPStmYlvq/WisHo1/JBXmrAxtWNGHmktMlxCqf6Iwy8MyYftU7TIR++c9Cz3g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yfvGfcQeoGgIX84+H9cRyTLS2ZefgcEUF6TFofmMYwiRjIJo9dp4Eq4cPWVv1SEh6Ob3Z2soEn96KgyVS7QHJA==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText4125397997870231769" style="display:none">Kristen Ashley was born in Gary, Indiana, USA. She nearly killed her mother and herself making it into the world, seeing as she had the umbilical cord wrapped around her neck (already attempting to accessorise and she hadn't taken her first breath!). <br /><br />Kristen grew up in Brownsburg, Indiana but has lived in Denver, Colorado and the West Country of England. Thus she has been blessed to have friends and family around the globe. Her posse is loopy (to say the least) but loopy is good when you want to write.<br /><br />Kristen was raised in a house with a large and multi-generational family. They lived on a very small farm in a small town in the heartland and existed amongst the strains of Glenn Miller, The Everly Brothers, REO Speedwagon and Whitesnake (and the wardrobes that matched).<br /><br />Needless to say, growing up in a house full of music, clothes and love was a good way to grow up. <br /><br />And as she keeps growing up, it keeps getting better.</span>
